                                       Attachment B




  GROUND LEASE AND CONSTRUCTION

            AGREEMENT

            By and Between

FAIR OAKS RECREATION & PARK DISTRICT

                 and

  SAN JUAN UNIFIED SCHOOL DISTRICT




                  15
                                                      51
        This Ground Lease and Construction Agreement (“Agreement”) is entered into as of
___________________ (“Effective Date”), by and between Fair Oaks Recreation & Park District,
a public recreation and park district and a political subdivision of the State of California (“FORPD”
or “Lessee”), and the San Juan Unified School District, a political subdivision of the State of
California (“District” or “Lessor”).

                                           RECITALS

        The Parties enter into this Agreement on the basis of the following facts, understandings
and intentions:

           A. District owns real property located at 4501 Bannister Rd. Fair Oaks, CA 95628
              (“Site”), as more fully described in Exhibit A and depicted in Exhibit B; and

           B. California Education Code sections 10900, et seq., empower District and FORPD
              to cooperate with each other and enter into agreements for the purpose of
              organizing, promoting, and conducting programs for community recreation;
              establishing a system of playgrounds and recreation; and acquiring, constructing,
              improving, maintaining, and operating recreational centers; and

           C. Education Code section 17077.40 explicitly authorizes the District to use grants to
              fund certain projects where the facilities are used jointly for both school and
              community purposes and therefore it is reasonable to understand, given the
              permissive education code, that other joint use arrangements are appropriate; and

           D. The District and FORPD entered into an agreement for the joint use and
              maintenance of the Site among other District and FORPD properties on September
              1, 2019 (“Joint Use Agreement”); and

           E. Section 12 of the Joint Use Agreement between the Parties permits FORPD to make
              capital improvements to the facilities and sites that are covered by the Joint Use
              Agreement; and

            F. FORPD desires to develop a portion of the Site as further depicted in Exhibit
               “C” (“Property”) by constructing softball fields, new parking lot, restroom
               and associated park amenities; and

           G. District and FORPD have evaluated the design and construction of the softball
              fields, parking lot, restroom and associated park amenities on the Site, for joint use
              by FORPD and the District to serve the families, children, and District students in
              the surrounding communities; and

           H. The Parties desire to contract for FORPD to construct the softball fields, parking
              lot, restroom and associated park amenities and to concurrently amend the existing
              Joint Use Agreement so that such amended Joint Use Agreement also governs the
              use and maintenance of the new facilities.



                                                 1
                                                 16
                                                                                                        52
           I. District and FORPD enter into this Agreement to set forth the terms and conditions
              upon with the Facilities (defined below) will be designed, constructed, operated and
              maintained by the Parties on the Site.

           J. District and FORPD intend for this Agreement to apply only to the lease of the
              Facilities and the construction of new Facilities. The Parties do not intend for this
              Agreement to modify, alter, or limit in any way the rights and obligations set out in
              the Joint Use Agreement, as amended. The Parties do not intend for the terms of
              this Agreement to impact any of the use of any of the sites in the Joint Use
              Agreement that are not the Property. The Parties intend that in the event of any
              irreconcilable conflict between the terms of this Agreement and the amended Joint
              Use Agreement, the terms of the amended Joint Use Agreement shall control.

                                          AGREEMENT

        NOW, THEREFORE, based on the foregoing Recitals, which are incorporated into this
Agreement by this reference, and the covenants and promises hereinafter contained, and for other
valuable consideration, the receipt and sufficiency of which are hereby acknowledged, the Parties
hereto agree as follows:

1.0    DEFINITIONS

       The following terms as used in this Agreement shall have the meanings given unless
expressly provided to the contrary:

       1.1      The term “Approved Plans” means all of the plans, permits, and approvals required
to construct the Project, including, but not limited to, all permits and approvals as are required by
Sections 3.4 and 3.8 below.

       1.2     The term “Completion” means the point where (1) FORPD’s contractor has fully
and correctly performed all work in all parts and requirements, including corrective and punch list
work as per the contractor’s Construction Contract with FORPD, and (2) District’s representatives
have conducted a final inspection that confirmed this performance.

        1.3     The term “Construction Contract” means the construction contract for the Project
to be entered into by FORPD and a contractor.

        1.4    The term “DSA” means the California Department of General Services, Division
of State Architect.

        1.5     The term “Facilities” means the buildings, structures, common areas, recreational
areas and other improvements constructed, installed, or placed as part of the Project and any other
improvements or alterations performed by FORPD on the Site pursuant to the terms of and during
the term of the Agreement.

       1.6     The term “Hazardous Materials” means any substance, material, or waste which is,
or becomes, regulated by any local, county or regional governmental authority, the State of
California, or the United States Government, including, but not limited to, any material or

                                                 2
                                                 17
                                                                                                        53
substance which is (i) defined as a “hazardous waste”, “extremely hazardous waste”, or “restricted
hazardous waste” under Section 25115, 25117 or 25122.7, or listed pursuant to Section 25140 of
the California Health and Safety Code, Division 20, Chapter 6.5 (Hazardous Waste Control Law),
(ii) defined as a “hazardous substance” under Section 25316 of the California Health and Safety
Code, Division 20, Chapter 6.8 (Carpenter-Presley-Tanner Hazardous Substance Account Act),
(iii) defined as a “hazardous material,” “hazardous substance,” or “hazardous waste” under Section
25501 of the California Health and Safety Code, Division 20, Chapter 6.95 (Hazardous Materials
Release Response Plans and Inventory), (iv) defined as a “hazardous substance” under Section
25281 of the California Health and Safety Code, Division 20, Chapter 6.7 (Underground Storage
of Hazardous Substances), (v) petroleum, (vi) friable asbestos, (vii) polychlorinated biphenyls,
(viii) methyl tertiary butyl ether, (ix) listed under Article 9 or defined as “hazardous” or “extremely
hazardous” pursuant to Article 11 of Title 22 of the California Administrative Code, Division 4,
Chapter 20, (x) designated as “hazardous substances” pursuant to Section 311 of the Clean Water
Act (33 U.S.C. §1317), (xi) defined as a “hazardous waste” pursuant to Section 1004 of the
Resource Conservation and Recovery Act, 42 U.S.C. §6901 et seq. (42 U.S.C. §6903) or (xii)
defined as “hazardous substances” pursuant to Section 101 of the Comprehensive Environmental
Response, Compensation, and Liability Act, 42 U.S.C. §9601 et seq.

        1.7      The term “Project” means the design and construction of the Facilities, including
softball fields,parking lot, restroom and associated park amenities all as more particularly set forth
in the description set forth in Exhibit “D” to this Agreement.

2.0    LEASE OF THE PROPERTY

        2.1     Lease Term. District leases the Property to FORPD for a term beginning on the
Effective Date, and expiring at 11:59 p.m. on the day immediately preceding the twenty-five (25)
year anniversary of the Effective Date (“Expiration Date”). Upon the Expiration Date, FORPD
may renew this Agreement for an additional twenty-five (25) year term (“Renewal Period”) at its
sole discretion. In order to renew this Agreement for the Renewal Period, FORPD shall provide
the District written notice of such intent to renew in the manner provided for in Section 6.1 of this
Agreement. At the end of the Renewal Period this Agreement shall terminate unless extended by
written mutual agreement of the parties or earlier terminated pursuant to the terms of this
Agreement.

       2.2     Option to Purchase. Upon the Expiration Date or upon the earlier termination of
this Agreement as defined herein, the District may extend to FORPD the option to purchase the
Property as defined herein. If the District offers the FORPD the option to purchase the Property,
then the Parties will, in good faith, commence negotiations for the sale and acquisition of the
Property for a mutually satisfactory sales price and terms in accordance with applicable state laws.
However, in the event the Parties cannot agree on a mutually satisfactory sales prices and terms,
this Agreement does not create an obligation that the District sell the Property FORPD, nor does
this Agreement create an obligation that FORPD purchase the Property from the District. If
FORPD elects to not purchase the Property or if the District elects to not offer the Property for
purchase, the District shall either terminate or renew this Agreement according to the provisions
described herein.



                                                  3
                                                  18
                                                                                                          54
        2.3     Joint Use Agreement. The District and FORPD have entered into a Joint Use
Agreement and the Parties have amended the Joint Use Agreement concurrent with the approval
of this Agreement. The Joint Use Agreement, as amended (the “Amended Joint Use Agreement”),
is attached as Exhibit E and it shall govern the relationship of the Parties for the use, management,
operation, and maintenance of the Facilities. The terms of this Agreement shall govern only the
lease of the Facilities, the performance of Project, and Completion of the Project as defined herein.
The use, management, operation, maintenance, and any other terms related to the Facilities and
the relationship between the Parties shall be governed by the Amended Joint Use Agreement.

        2.4     AS-IS Condition. Except to the extent of the express covenants of the District set
forth in this Agreement, FORPD accepts the Property in its present condition notwithstanding the
fact that there may be certain defects in the Property, whether or not known to either Party to this
Agreement at the time of the execution of this Agreement by FORPD, and FORPD hereby
represents that it has performed all investigations it deems necessary, including, without limitation,
soils and engineering inspections, in connection with its acceptance of the Property “AS IS”.

      2.5     Rent. FORPD shall pay to District annual rent for each year of the lease term of
One Dollar ($1), payable annually on the Effective Date of this Agreement.

        2.6     Permitted Uses of Property. FORPD will use the Property primarily for the purpose
of constructing, operating, maintaining, managing, and using the Project and Facilities to provide
the community recreation, park, and sports programs and services (which may include a food and
drink concession) and joint uses by District in accordance with the terms of the Amended Joint
Use Agreement. Except as specifically provided herein, the Property shall be used for no other
purpose without the prior written consent of District. FORPD shall obtain and maintain all
required state and local licenses and permits required for FORPD to use and provide the
community recreation, park, and sports programs and services on the Property, and District agrees
to cooperate with FORPD in obtaining and maintaining such permits, to the extent that District’s
cooperation is reasonably necessary in connection with the same. FORPD shall materially comply
with all applicable laws with respect to its use of the Property. FORPD shall, and shall use
commercially reasonable efforts to ensure that, its directors, officers, agents, employees, invitees,
volunteers and independent contractors observe and comply fully and faithfully with all reasonable
and nondiscriminatory rules and regulations including all policies adopted by District related to
the joint use of the Property; provided that such rules and regulations are consistent with those
rules and regulations currently related to the joint use of the Property.

       2.7     Prohibited Uses of Property.

                2.7.1 FORPD shall not conduct or knowingly permit to be conducted any private
or public nuisance on or about the Property, nor commit any active, physical waste thereon. No
rubbish, trash, waste, residue, brush, weeds or undergrowth or debris of any kind or character shall
ever be placed or permitted to accumulate upon any portion of the Site, except in appropriate
receptacles intended for such purposes, nor shall FORPD knowingly permit any portion of the
Property to be maintained so as to render the Property a fire hazard or an imminent risk to public
health and safety.



                                                  4
                                                  19
                                                                                                         55
                 2.7.2 No condition shall be permitted to exist upon the Property which shall
induce, breed or harbor infectious plant diseases, rodents, or noxious insects and FORPD shall
take such measures as are appropriate to prevent any conditions from existing on the Property
which create a danger to the health or safety of any persons residing or working at, or persons
visiting, the Site.

               2.7.3 No materially adverse environmental condition in violation of applicable
laws shall be permitted to exist on any portion of the Property, nor shall any Hazardous Materials
be permitted to be generated, treated, stored, disposed of, or otherwise deposited in or on or
allowed to emanate from the Site or any portion thereof; provided, however, thatHazardous
Materials may be stored or used, so long as such storage and use is (a) ancillary to the ordinary use
and maintenance of the Property with the intent that such material will be used in the ordinary
course of business, and (b) conducted in compliance with all applicable laws.

        2.8    Improvements and Alterations. Except as otherwise expressly provided in this
Agreement, no structures, improvements, alterations, or facilities shall be constructed, erected,
altered, or made by FORPD at or upon the Property without the prior written consent of District,
which consent shall not be unreasonably withheld, delayed or denied.

       2.9     Ownership of Improvements during Term. Until the Expiration Date or sooner
termination of this Agreement, FORPD shall own all Facilities and other improvements hereafter
constructed, installed, or placed by FORPD upon the Property, and all alterations, additions, or
betterments made thereto by FORPD.

         2.10 Reversion of Improvements. Upon the Expiration Date or sooner termination of
this Agreement in accordance with terms hereof, whether by cancellation, forfeiture or otherwise,
(a) all structures, buildings, and other real property fixtures made to or upon the Property shall
remain upon the Site as part thereof, and title thereto shall revert to District, and (b) FORPD shall
retain ownership of, and remove and relocate to other FORPD land, all equipment, apparatus,
removable structures, and other personal property installed or placed on the Property by FORPD.

        2.11 Assignment and Subletting. FORPD may not assign this Agreement, or any part
thereof, or sublet any portion of the Site without District’s prior written consent, which consent
shall not be unreasonably withheld, delayed or denied. Except as provided herein, no assignment
or transfer shall be effective unless and until the proposed assignee executes and delivers to District
an agreement, in a form reasonably satisfactory to District, assuming FORPD’s obligations that
have been specifically assigned. Thereafter, FORPD shall be relieved of all responsibility to
District for performance of the obligations assumed by the assignee. The Parties acknowledge that
FORPD may contract with a concessionaire to operate and manage a food/drink concession on the
Property and agree that such a concessionaire agreement will not be considered a sublease within
the meaning of this section.

        2.12 Taxes and Assessments. Pursuant to Section 107.6 of the California Revenue and
Taxation Code (“Code”), District hereby notifies FORPD that: (i) a possessory interest with
respect to the Property is created and/or continued pursuant to the Agreement (“Possessory
Interest”) and may be subject to property taxation under the Code; and (ii) FORPD may be subject
to, and shall bear, the payment of all property taxes and related charges and expenses attributable

                                                  5
                                                  20
                                                                                                          56
to all periods during the term of this Agreement with respect to the Possessory Interest
(collectively, “Taxes”). FORPD shall indemnify, defend and hold harmless District against all
such Taxes (with respect to the Possessory Interest only) which may become payable by District
during the term of this Agreement.

        2.13 Inspection. District reserves and shall at any and all reasonable times, upon twenty-
four (24) hours’ notice to FORPD, have the right to enter the Property to inspect same, to determine
whether FORPD is complying with this Agreement, and to fulfill District’s obligations to FORPD
hereunder. FORPD waives any claim for damages for injury, inconvenience, or interference, or
any loss of occupancy or quiet enjoyment, caused by such entry, except to the extent caused by
the gross negligence, recklessness or willful misconduct of District or any person or entity entering
upon the Property under District’s direction or control.

        2.14 Hazardous Material. Except to the extent caused by District, or caused by and/or
emanating from other property owned by District, the District shall not be responsible for the
presence of any Hazardous Materials placed, stored, or used on the Property by FORPD
subsequent to the Effective Date of this Agreement or for the cost of any environmental clean-up
or other necessary or required remediation with respect thereto. It shall be the sole responsibility
of FORPD to investigate all aspects of the physical condition of the Property, including, but not
limited to, the existence of any Hazardous Materials, and earthquake faults or other geologic
hazards. FORPD shall indemnify, defend, and hold District harmless from any claim, suit, or
action arising from the presence of any Hazardous Materials placed, stored, or used on the Property
by FORPD subsequent to the Effective Date, and from any claim, suit, or action arising from any
environmental clean-up or remediation with respect thereto; provided, however, that the above
shall not apply to the extent caused by District, or caused by and/or emanating from other property
owned by the District.

        2.15 Title Reservations. FORPD expressly agrees that this Agreement and all rights
hereunder shall be subject to all encumbrances, reservations, licenses, easements and rights of way
of record (a) existing as of the Effective Date, or (b) otherwise referenced in this Agreement in, to,
over or affecting the Property for any purpose whatsoever, or (c) consented to in writing by
FORPD. Notwithstanding the foregoing or anything herein to the contrary, District agrees to
reasonably cooperate with FORPD in FORPD’s efforts to address title matters, if any, which would
prevent FORPD from proceeding with the development, construction, or use of the Project.

3.0    DESIGN AND CONSTRUCTION OF PROJECT

       3.1     Construction Costs. Except as otherwise agreed between the parties, all costs to
construct the Project shall be paid by FORPD. Such costs shall include, but not be limited to,
Project design, title review, site testing and inspection, all required permits, governmental
approvals, environmental review, construction, inspection, close-out, and Project management
(“Project Costs”).

       3.2     Evidence of Financing. FORPD shall provide District with written notice,
reasonably satisfactory to District in its reasonable discretion, that FORPD has the funding or
secured the financing necessary to pay the Project Costs (“Financing Notice”) on or before
[______________] (“Financing Notice Date”). District acknowledges that reasonably satisfactory

                                                  6
                                                  21
                                                                                                         57
evidence of funding or financing includes, without limitation, pledges made by FORPD
benefactors, copies of relevant portions of final notes, guarantees, partnership, shareholder or
limited liability company agreements, construction loan and/or permanent loan commitments, or
financial statements. If FORPD fails to provide the Financing Notice by the Financing Notice
Date, District may, in its reasonable discretion, terminate this Agreement. District shall provide
FORPD with written notice of termination, which notice shall be effective the thirtieth (30th)
calendar day from the date of the written notice.

        3.3     Permits and Approvals. Subject to Section 3.5, prior to commencement of
construction of the Project, FORPD shall, at its sole cost and expense, obtain all permits and
approvals required to commence construction by any governmental agency with jurisdiction over
all or portions of the Project.

        3.4     District Cooperation. District shall cooperate with and assist FORPD, to the extent
reasonably requested by FORPD, in FORPD's efforts to obtain the appropriate governmental
approvals, consents, permits or variances which may be required in connection with the
procurement of the approvals and permits for the Project (including, without limitation, applying
for such permits in District’s name). Such cooperative efforts may, without limitation, include
District’s joinder in any application for such approval, consent, permit or variance, where joinder
therein by District is required; provided, however, that FORPD shall reimburse District for the
actual costs incurred by District in connection with such joinder or cooperative efforts.

        3.5     Environmental Review. The Project is a project subject to the California
Environmental Quality Act (“CEQA”). FORPD shall be the lead agency with respect to
environmental review under CEQA for the Project. FORPD shall prepare and complete any
environmental studies and documents required pursuant to CEQA. FORPD shall be responsible
for costs incurred in performing all required environmental review of the Project, including but
not limited to the costs to retain all consultants. If, during or upon completion of environmental
review, either Party determines that the Project is not feasible, either Party may terminate this
Agreement upon thirty (30) calendar days’ written notice to the other Party.

        3.6     Schematic Plans. FORPD shall hire and retain an architect (the “Project Architect”)
to prepare and submit a schematic design for the Project to District. Within thirty (30) days of
District’s receipt of the schematic design, District shall approve the schematic design or provide
FORPD with District’s comments and revisions. FORPD shall consider District’s written
comments and revisions and resubmit the schematic design to District for approval. Within fifteen
(15) days of FORPD’s resubmittal, District shall approve the schematic design or provide FORPD
with District’s comments and revisions. District’s approval under this section shall not be
unreasonably conditioned, delayed or denied.

        3.7     Plans, Drawings, and Specifications. All material meetings with the Project
Architect shall be coordinated with District to ensure that one (1) or more District representatives
will be available to attend. FORPD shall submit the final plans to District for review and approval,
which approval shall not be unreasonably delayed, withheld or denied. All plans, drawings, and
specifications shall be prepared by a licensed professional.



                                                 7
                                                 22
                                                                                                       58
        3.8     Construction in Accordance with Approved Plans/Project Inspector. The Project
shall be constructed in material compliance with this Agreement and the Approved Plans. FORPD
shall retain a project inspector qualified and approved by DSA to perform the duties of and act as
the general building inspector for the Project. The inspector shall perform the duties of an
inspector as specified in California Education Code Sections 17309 and 17311 and Sections 4-333
and 4-342 of Title 24 of the California Code of Regulations.

        3.9     Construction Schedule. Construction of the Project may not commence until (a)
completion of the Approved Plans, (b) District approval of the Financing Notice, (c) FORPD has
obtained all required governmental permits and approvals to commence construction of the
Project, (d) completion of environmental review pursuant to Section 3.5, and (e) provision of the
insurance policies or additional insured certificates required by Section 3.18 (collectively, the
“Construction Pre-Conditions”). District shall provide FORPD with written notice of its approval
for FORPD to proceed (“NOP”) with construction within thirty (30) business days of the
satisfaction of all of the Construction Pre-Conditions. District’s delivery of the NOP shall
constitute District’s approval of the satisfaction of the Construction Pre-Conditions or its waiver
of the requirement to satisfy the same. FORPD shall achieve Completion within eighteen (18)
months after District’s issuance of the NOP to FORPD. Once construction is commenced, it shall
be diligently pursued to Completion, and shall not be abandoned for more than one hundred twenty
(120) consecutive days, except as set forth in Sections 5.7 and 6.15.

        3.10 Rights of Access during Construction. District representatives shall, upon twenty-
four (24) hours’ notice to FORPD and at reasonable times during normal business hours, have the
right of reasonable access to the Property for the purpose of ascertaining compliance with the terms
and conditions of this Agreement, including but not limited to the inspection of the construction
work being performed. Such access shall be reasonably calculated to minimize interference with
FORPD's construction and/or operations, and District shall comply with all applicable industry
safety standards in connection with any such access. FORPD shall have the right to have a
representative present to accompany the District representatives in connection with such access.

         3.11 Notice of Completion/Close-out. Upon Completion of the Project, FORPD shall
file or cause to be filed a timely Notice of Completion (“Notice of Completion”). FORPD shall
also file or cause to be filed all close-out forms or documents reasonably required by DSA.

        3.12 As-Built Plans. Upon Completion of the Project, FORPD shall deliver or cause to
be delivered to District, at no cost to District, two (2) sets of reproducible final as-built plans and
specifications of the Project as well as a link to a websitecontaining the final as-built plans and
specifications.

        3.13 Use and Re-Use of Plans. FORPD shall use commercially reasonable efforts to
ensure that contracts between FORPD and any architect, design professional or licensed contractor
in connection with Project shall provide, in form and content reasonably satisfactory to District,
for the assignment of any final, stamped Project-related plans and specifications to District upon
any termination or expiration of this Agreement. Upon any such termination or expiration, District
may, at its election, to the extent permitted by the underlying contract, use any such plans and
specifications created by such architect, design professional or contractor in connection with such
contract and the Project. If District reuses any Project-related plans or specifications, then District

                                                  8
                                                  23
                                                                                                          59
shall hold FORPD harmless against all claims, damages, losses, and expenses arising from such
reuse.

       3.14 Protection of District. Nothing in this Agreement shall be construed as giving
FORPD or any other person any right, power or authority to act as agent of or to contract for, or
permit the rendering of, any services, or the furnishing of any materials, in any such manner as
would give rise to the filing of mechanics' liens or other claims against District’s interest in the
Property.

         3.15 Prompt Payment. FORPD shall carry out the construction of the Project in
conformity with all applicable federal and state labor laws, including, without limitation, the
requirement under California law to pay prevailing wages and hire apprentices. FORPD shall be
solely responsible for determining and effectuating compliance with such laws. FORPD shall
indemnify, protect, defend and hold harmless District from and against any and all out-of-pocket
loss, liability, damage, claim, cost, expense and/or “increased costs” (as defined in Labor Code
section 1781) (including reasonable attorneys’ fees, court and litigation costs, and fees of expert
witnesses but excluding lost profits, lost opportunities and other consequential, special or punitive
damages) arising out of or in connection with the construction of the Project, including, without
limitation, any of the following: (1) the noncompliance by FORPD or its contractors of any
applicable local, state and/or federal law, including, without limitation, any applicable federal
and/or state labor laws (including, without limitation, if applicable, the requirement to pay state
prevailing wages and hire apprentices); and (2) the implementation of Section 1781 of the Labor
Code, as the same may be amended from time to time, or any other similar law. The foregoing
indemnity shall survive termination of this Agreement and shall continue after Completion of the
construction of the Project by FORPD.

         3.16 Liens. Subject to FORPD's rights to contest the same prior to payment, FORPD
shall keep the Property and any improvements thereon free and clear of all stop notice liens and
other liens arising out of or in connection with work done for FORPD and/or any parties claiming
through FORPD. FORPD agrees to and shall indemnify, defend and hold District harmless from
and against any claim, liability, out-of-pocket loss, damages, costs, expenses, reasonable attorneys'
fees incurred in defending, and all other expenses on account of claims of lien(s) of laborers or
materialmen or others for work performed or materials or supplies furnished to FORPD or persons
claiming under it. (excluding lost profits, lost opportunities and other consequential, special or
punitive damages). In the event any stop notice lien or other lien arising out of or in connection
with work done for FORPD and/or any parties claiming through FORPD is recorded against the
Property, FORPD shall, within the later of (a) thirty (30) days after the recording of such lien, or
(b) five (5) business days after written demand from District is delivered to FORPD, furnish any
one of the following, as determined by FORPD: (i) the bond described in California Civil Code
Section 9364, or successor statute, which results in the removal of such lien from the Property, (ii)
a set aside letter from FORPD's construction lender, in form and substance reasonably satisfactory
to District, setting aside sufficient funds from FORPD's construction loan for the satisfaction of
such lien, (iii) a title insurance policy or endorsement insuring District against any loss or liability
arising out of such lien, together with any other evidence requested by District to evidence that
such claim will be paid, removed or discharged as a claim against the Property and/or District, or
(iv) otherwise satisfy and extinguish the lien.


                                                   9
                                                  24
                                                                                                           60
         3.17 Project Indemnification. For the purposes of the Project and until Completion
thereof, FORPD shall indemnify, defend, and hold District, its Board (collectively and each
individual member), employees, and agents harmless from and against all out-of-pocket liabilities,
losses, damages, costs and expenses, including reasonable attorney’s fees, expert witness fees, and
court costs (excluding lost profits, lost opportunities and other consequential, special or punitive
damages) (hereinafter, collectively, “Claims”), arising from or as a result of the death or injury to
any person or any accident, injury, loss, or damage whatsoever caused to any person or to the
property of any person and which is caused by any acts or any errors or omissions of FORPD or
any of its employees, agents, servants, invitees, contractors, or subcontractors arising from, related
to, or connected with the construction of the Project; provided, however, FORPD shall not be
required to indemnify, defend, and hold harmless for a Claim arising under this section if the Claim
arises from or is caused solely by the acts, omissions, or errors of the entity or person seeking such
indemnification or defense. District shall indemnify, defend, and hold FORPD, its Board
(collectively and each individual member), employees, and agents harmless from and against all
Claims, arising from or as a result of the death or injury to any person or any accident, injury, loss,
or damage whatsoever caused to any person or to the property of any person and which is caused
by any acts or any errors or omissions of District or any of its employees, agents, servants, invitees,
contractors, or subcontractors arising from, related to, or connected with the construction of the
Project; provided, however, District shall not be required to indemnify, defend, and hold harmless
for a Claim arising under this section if the Claim arises from or is caused solely by the acts,
omissions, or errors of the entity or person seeking such indemnification or defense. Upon
Completion of the Project the indemnity provided for in the Amended Joint Use Agreement shall
control.

       3.18 Insurance during Construction. During the construction of the Project, FORPD
shall obtain and maintain, or require the Project contractor or other consultants to obtain and
maintain, the following insurance or self-insurance coverages:

                3.18.1 Builder's Risk. This insurance shall be endorsed to include ordinance or
law coverage, coverage for temporary offsite storage, debris removal, pollutant cleanup and
removal, testing, preservation of property, excavation costs, landscaping, shrubs and plants and
full collapse coverage during construction without restricting collapse coverage to specified perils.
This insurance shall be written on a completed-value basis and cover the entire value of the Project.

               3.18.2 General Liability. FORPD shall maintain general liability insurance with
coverage at least as broad as Insurance Services Office (ISO) form CG 00 01, in an amount not
less than Three Million Dollars ($3,000,000) per occurrence for bodily injury, personal injury, and
property damage. If a general aggregate limit applies, either the general aggregate limit shall apply
separately to this project/location or the general aggregate limit shall be twice the required
occurrence limit. FORPD’s general liability policies shall be primary and shall not seek
contribution from the District’s coverage.

                3.18.3 Automobile Liability. This insurance shall be written with a limit of
liability of not less than One Million Dollars ($1,000,000) per occurrence and aggregate. The
insurance shall include coverage for all “owned,” “hired” and “non-owned” automobiles, or
coverage for “any auto.”


                                                  10
                                                  25
                                                                                                          61
                3.18.4 Professional Liability. This insurance shall cover liability arising from any
error, omission, negligent or wrongful act of the contractor and/or licensed professional (i.e.
architects, engineers, surveyors, etc.). This coverage shall also provide an extended three (3) year
reporting period commencing upon termination or cancellation of the Project. The limits of the
coverage shall be Three Million Dollars ($3,000,000) with respect to the Architect for the Project.

                 3.18.5 Additional Insured. The general liability and automobile liability insurance
coverage shall name District as an additional insured. A duplicate policy or policies (or certificates
of insurance) evidencing the insurance coverage, in such form as shall be reasonably acceptable to
District, shall be provided to District prior to the commencement of construction. The policy or
policies of insurance shall provide that such insurance coverage will not be canceled or reduced
without at least thirty (30) days prior written notice to Lessor or ten (10) business days in case of
cancellation for failure to pay the premium. At least ten (10) business days prior to the expiration
of such policy, a certificate showing that such insurance coverage has been renewed shall be
obtained by FORPD and filed with District.

       3.19 Antidiscrimination during Construction. FORPD by and for itself and its
successors and assigns covenants that there shall be no discrimination against or segregation of a
person or of a group of persons on account of any basis listed in subdivision (a) or (d) of Section
12955 of the Government Code, as those bases are defined in Sections 12926, 12926.1, subdivision
(m) and paragraph (1) of subdivision (p) of Section 12955, and Section 12955.2 of the Government
Code, in the course of construction of the Project.

4.0    MAINTENANCE, OPERATION AND JOINT USE OF FACILITIES

      4.1     Ownership of Facilities. The Parties acknowledge and agree that the Facilities
ownership is governed by Sections 2.9 and 2.10.

      4.2      Joint Use of Facilities. District and FORPD shall jointly use Facilities in the
manner set forth in the Amended Joint Use Agreement.

        4.3    Maintenance and Repair. Maintenance and repair of the Facilities and related costs
shall be governed by the terms of the Amended Joint Use Agreement executed between the Parties.

        4.4      Damage and Destruction. If the Facilities or any part of them are destroyed or
substantially damaged by a fire, flood, or other risk occurrence, then FORPD may decide and elect
whether to repair and restore the destroyed or damaged Facilities. FORPD shall notify District
about its election in writing within 60 days following the date of the damage or destruction. If
FORPD elects to repair and restore the Facilities, then FORPD shall proceed to repair and restore
the Facilities on substantially the same plans and design that existed before the damage or
destruction and FORPD shall diligently proceed to complete the repairs and restoration (subject to
the availability of insurance proceeds or other funding). If FORPD elects not to repair and restore
the Facilities, then the Agreement and Amended Joint Use Agreement shall continue in effect as
to the remaining Facilities.




                                                 11
                                                  26
                                                                                                         62
5.0     DEFAULTS, REMEDIES AND TERMINATION

       5.1     Applicability. The terms contained within Section 5 shall only have force and effect
during the term of the Project as defined herein and agreed to by the Parties. The terms of this
Section 5 shall cease to have force and effect upon Completion of the Project. The terms of the
Amended Joint Use Agreement shall control commencing upon Completion and shall survive the
term of this Agreement.

        5.2       Defaults General. Subject to the extensions of time set forth in Sections 5.7 and
6.15 below, failure by either party to perform any material term or provision of this Agreement
constitutes a default under this Agreement; provided, however, the party shall not be deemed to be
in default if (i) such party cures, corrects, or remedies such default within thirty (30) business days
after receipt of a notice specifying such failure or delay, or (ii) for such defaults that cannot
reasonably be cured, corrected, or remedied within thirty (30) business days, if such party
commences to cure, correct, or remedy such failure or delay within thirty (30) business days after
receipt of a notice specifying such failure or delay, and diligently prosecutes such cure, correction,
or remedy to completion.

        5.3     Notice of Default. The party claiming breach shall give written notice of default to
the party in default, specifying the default with reasonable specificity. Except as required to
protect against further damages, the injured party may not institute proceedings against the party
in default until thirty (30) business days after giving such notice. Except as otherwise expressly
provided in this Agreement, any failure or delay in giving such notice or in asserting any of its
rights and remedies as to any default shall not constitute a waiver of any default, nor shall it change
the time of default, nor shall it deprive either party of its rights to institute and maintain any actions
or proceedings which it may deem necessary to protect, assert or enforce any such rights or
remedies.

         5.4     Legal Actions. In addition to any other rights or remedies and subject to the
restrictions set forth in this Agreement, either party may institute an action at law or in equity to
seek specific performance of the terms of this Agreement, or to cure, correct or remedy any default,
to recover damages for any default, or to obtain any other remedy consistent with the purpose of
this Agreement; provided, however, that notwithstanding anything in the foregoing to the contrary,
in no event shall either party be entitled to obtain monetary damages of any kind from the other
party, including, but not limited to, damages for economic loss, lost profits, or any other economic
or consequential damages of any kind, except for actual out-of-pocket costs incurred by the non-
defaulting party as a result of nonperformance of the defaulting party’s covenants under this
Agreement. Such legal actions must be instituted in the Superior Court of the State of California,
County of Sacramento.

        5.5    Rights and Remedies are Cumulative. Except as otherwise expressly stated in this
Agreement, the rights and remedies of the parties are cumulative, and the exercise by any party of
one or more of its rights or remedies shall not preclude the exercise by it, at the same or different
times, of any other rights or remedies for the same default or any other default by another party.

       5.6    Termination by District. Subject to Sections 5.2, 5.3, 5.7, and 6.15, the District
may terminate this Agreement if any of the following occurs:

                                                   12
                                                   27
                                                                                                             63
                               (i)    FORPD does not timely submit to District FORPD’s
                evidence of insurance pursuant to Section 3.18 ;

                               (ii)   FORPD fails to timely secure all of the approvals and
                permits required pursuant to Section 2.6 and Section 3.3;

                                (iii)   FORPD fails to timely commence construction of the
                Project;

                                (iv)    FORPD fails to timely achieve Completion of the Project;

                               (v)     FORPD transfers, assigns or sublets any of its rights or
                obligations under this Agreement in violation of Section 2.11;

                                (vi)     FORPD is the subject of any voluntary or involuntary
                proceeding in bankruptcy (which proceeding is not dismissed within sixty (60) days
                of the date of filing); or

                              (vii) FORPD is in default of any of the material covenants, terms,
                and conditions, including, but not limited to, FORPD’s obligation to pay rent, of
                this Agreement.

        In the event of any of the foregoing, District, at its option, may deliver a thirty (30) business
day written notice of termination to FORPD and, if the applicable requirement has not been
satisfied (or waived by District) within said time period, or such additional period of time as is
reasonably necessary to satisfy said requirement (provided FORPD commences to satisfy said
requirement within said thirty (30) business day period and diligently proceeds to satisfy said
requirement), this Agreement shall terminate. Termination under this Section 5.6 shall not have
any effect on the rights and obligations held by the Parties under the Amended Joint Use
Agreement. The Amended Joint Use Agreement and the terms contained therein shall survive the
termination of this Agreement.

         Termination by FORPD. In the event that FORPD is not in default under this Agreement
and, in addition to any other of FORPD’s right to terminate this Agreement, FORPD may terminate
this Agreement if District is in material breach of the terms of the Agreement or at FORPD’s
convenience prior to commencement of any construction on the Property. In such event, FORPD,
at its option, may deliver a thirty (30) business day written notice of termination to District and, if
the applicable requirement has not been satisfied (or waived by FORPD) within said time period,
or such additional period of time as is reasonably necessary to satisfy said requirement (provided
District commences to satisfy said requirement within said thirty (30) business day period and
diligently proceeds to satisfy said requirement), this Agreement shall terminate. Termination under
Section 5.6 shall not have any effect on the rights and obligations held by the Parties under the
Amended Joint Use Agreement. The Amended Joint Use Agreement and the terms contained
therein shall survive the termination of this Agreement.

        5.7    Force Majeure; Extensions of Time of Performance. In addition to specific
provisions of this Agreement, performance by either party hereunder shall not be deemed to be in
default where delays or defaults are due to war, insurrection, strikes, lock-outs, riots, floods,

                                                   13
                                                   28
                                                                                                            64
earthquakes, fires, casualties, Acts of God, acts of the public enemy, epidemics, quarantine
restrictions, freight embargoes, lack of transportation, governmental restrictions or priority,
litigation, inclement weather, inability to secure necessary labor, materials or tools, delays of any
contractor, subcontractor or supplier, acts of the other party, acts or failure to act by District or any
other public or governmental agency or entity (except that any act or failure to act of District shall
not excuse performance by District), or any other causes beyond the control or without the fault of
the party claiming an extension of time to perform. An extension of time for any such cause shall
be for the period of the enforced delay and shall commence to run from the time of the
commencement of the cause, if notice by the party claiming such extension is sent to the other
party within thirty (30) business days of knowledge of the commencement of the cause. A party
claiming delay under this provision shall use its best efforts to promptly implement a plan to ensure
the continued ability to perform its obligations and promptly bring to an end the force majeure
condition.

6.0     GENERAL PROVISIONS

        6.1      Notices. Notices, demands, and communications between FORPD and District
shall be sufficiently given if (a) personally delivered, or (b) delivered by a reputable document
delivery service that provides a receipt showing date and time of delivery, or (c) delivered by
United States mail, certified postage prepaid, return receipt requested, or (d) by email, provided
that such email shall be followed within one (1) business day by delivery of such notice pursuant
to clause (a), (b) or (c) above, to the offices of FORPD and District, as follows:

        Notices personally delivered or delivered by document delivery service shall be effective
upon receipt. Mailed notices shall be effective at the earlier of (i) Noon on the second business
day following deposit with the United States Postal Service, or (ii) actual delivery (whether
accepted or refused) as evidenced by printed confirmation if by email (provided that if any notice
or other communication to be delivered by email as provided above cannot be transmitted because
of a problem affecting the receiving party’s computer, the deadline for receiving such notice or
other communication shall be extended through the next business day), as shown by the
addressee’s return receipt if by certified mail, and as confirmed by the courier service if by courier;
provided, however, that if such actual delivery occurs after 5:00 p.m. (local time where received)
or on a non-business day, then such notice or communication so made shall be deemed effective
on the first (1st) business day after the day of actual delivery. Such written notices, demands, and
communications may be delivered or sent in the same manner to such other addresses as either
party may from time to time designate by written notice provided in accordance with this Section
6.1.

         6.2     Quiet Enjoyment. On FORPD's observation and performance of all of the
covenants, terms, and conditions of this Agreement to be observed and performed by FORPD,
FORPD shall peaceably and quietly hold and enjoy the Property from and after its delivery to
FORPD without disturbance from District; this is subject, however, to (a) the rights of the parties
as set forth in this Agreement, and (b) the terms of any instruments or encumbrances to which this
Agreement is subordinate.

       6.3     Independent Contractors. Neither Party, nor its employees, agents, officers, or
representatives, shall be deemed employees, agents, officers, or representatives of the other Party.

        6.4     Conflicts of Interest. No member, official, officer, employee, agent, representative,
or consultant of District shall have any personal interest, direct or indirect, in this Agreement nor
shall any such member, official, officer, agent, representative, or employee participate in any
decision relating to this Agreement which affects his or her personal interests or the interests of
any corporation, partnership, or association in which he or she has a direct or indirect interest.
District warrants that it has not paid or given, and will not pay or give, any such member, official,


                                                  15
                                                  30
                                                                                                          66
officer, employee, agent, representative, or consultant of FORPD any money or other
consideration for obtaining this Agreement.

        6.5   Execution in Counterparts. This Agreement may be executed in counterparts, each
of which, when this Agreement has been signed by all the parties hereto, shall be deemed to be an
original.

        6.6     Entire Agreement. This Agreement constitutes the entire understanding and
agreement of the parties and integrates all of the terms and conditions mentioned herein or
incidental hereto and supersedes all negotiations or previous agreements between the parties with
respect to the subject matter hereof.

       6.7     Conflicting Terms. In the event of any irreconcilable inconsistency or conflict
between the Agreement and the Amended Joint Use Agreement, the terms, conditions and
provisions of the Amended Joint Use Agreement shall govern and control.

       6.8     Third Party Beneficiaries. Nothing in this Agreement is intended to create any third
party beneficiaries to this Agreement.

       6.9     Waivers. All waivers of the provisions of this Agreement must be in writing and
signed by the appropriate authorities of FORPD or District, and all amendments hereto must be in
writing and signed by the appropriate authorities of FORPD and District.

       6.10 Amendment. This Agreement and any provisions hereof may only be amended by
mutual written agreement executed by authorized representatives of District and FORPD.
Amendment of this Agreement by either Party is only effective upon approval of such amendment
by each Party’s Governing Board..

       6.11 Governing Law. This Agreement shall be governed by and construed in accordance
with the laws of the State of California.

        6.12 Severability. If any provision of this Agreement is held invalid, void, or
unenforceable by a court of competent jurisdiction, but the remainder of the Agreement can be
enforced without failure of material consideration to any Party, then this Agreement shall not be
affected and it shall remain in full force and effect, unless amended or modified by mutual consent
of the Parties; provided, however, that if the invalidity or unenforceability of any provision of this
Agreement results in a material failure of consideration, then the Party adversely affected thereby
shall have the right in its reasonable discretion to terminate this Agreement upon providing 30-day
prior written notice of such termination to the other Party.

        6.13 Warranty of Authority. Each of the persons signing this Agreement represents and
warrants that such person has been duly authorized to sign this Agreement on behalf of the Party
indicated, and each of the Parties by signing this Agreement warrants and represents that such
Party is legally authorized and entitled to enter into this Agreement.

        6.14 Recording. Unless the parties agree otherwise in writing in advance, on or before
the Effective Date, FORPD and District shall execute a Memorandum of Lease substantially in the
form of Exhibit “F” attached hereto (the “Memorandum of Lease”). At FORPD’s option, FORPD

                                                 16
                                                  31
                                                                                                         67
shall cause the Memorandum of Lease to be recorded at FORPD’s sole cost and District shall be
solely responsible for any transfer taxes or fees required to be paid in connection with the recording
of the Memorandum of Lease.

       6.15 Deadlines. The deadlines and time periods in the Agreement may be extended or
modified by mutual written consent of the Parties.

AMENDED JOINT USE AGREEMENT




            38

                                       AMENDMENT NO. 1
                                  TO JOINT USE AGREEMENT


        THIS AMENDMENT TO AGREEMENT is entered into as of _____________, 2022 by and
between Fair Oaks Recreation & Park District, a public recreation and park district and a
political subdivision of the State of California (“FORPD”), and San Juan Unified School District,
a political subdivision of the State of California (“District”).

1. Recitals. This Amendment is made with reference to the following background recitals:

   1.1.     On September 1, 2019, the parties entered into the Joint Use Agreement (the
“Agreement”), which is on file in the District office, concerning the joint use of FORPD and
District facilities.

    1.2.     Concurrent with the approval of this Amendment, the parties have approved the
Ground Lease and Construction Agreement (“Lease”) concerning the lease and construction of
facilities by FORPD at District’s La Vista site located at 4501 Bannister Road, Fair Oaks, CA
95628. The Lease provides that the parties will amend the Agreement concurrent with the
approval of the Lease. The Lease further provides that the Lease will govern the lease, design,
and construction of new facilities at the La Vista site, and that the amended Agreement will
govern the relationship of the parties regarding the use, management, operation, and maintenance
of the facilities at the La Vista site.

   1.3.  The parties acknowledge that the Lease is a “separate agreement” governing
improvement to District property within the meaning of Agreement section 12.

    1.4.   The parties now desire to amend the Agreement concurrent with the parties’ approval
of the Lease. The parties intend for this Amendment to set forth new and modified Agreement
terms specific to the La Vista site.

2. Definitions. The following terms shall have these meanings for purposes of this Amendment:

   2.1.    “La Vista Facilities” mean “Facilities” as that term is defined in the Lease.

   2.2.    “La Vista Property” means “Property” as that term is defined in the Lease.

3. Amendments to Agreement. The parties amend the Agreement as follows:

    3.1.   Agreement sections 1 and 4(b) are modified to add the following provision relating to
the La Vista Facilities and La Vista Property:

       The Facilities include the La Vista Facilities to be constructed and installed by FORPD
       under the terms of the Lease. FORPD shall operate, manage, maintain, and repair the La
       Vista Facilities and control and manage the use of the La Vista Facilities, including the
       scheduling of such use. FORPD shall be the principal user of the La Vista Facilities and
       shall have the first and senior priority to such use at all times. FORPD may use the La



                                                39
                                                                                                    75
       Vista Facilities for adult recreational programs subject to the terms of the Agreement.
       District may use the La Vista Facilities only when such use would not interfere with
       FORPD use. Any District use must be scheduled through and approved by FORPD.

   3.2.     Agreement section 2 is modified to add the following provision relating to the La
Vista Facilities and La Vista Property:

       The Agreement term as applied to FORPD’s use of the La Vista Facilities and La Vista
       Property shall be concurrent with the term of the Lease. If the Lease is terminated or
       expires, the Agreement term shall revert to Agreement section 2.

    3.3.     Agreement section 3 is modified to incorporate the Lease as an additional contract
that sets forth the parties’ understanding relating to the Facilities.

   3.4.     Agreement section 5 is modified to add the following provision relating to the La
Vista Facilities and La Vista Property:

       FORPD at its cost shall operate, manage, maintain, and repair the La Vista Facilities and
       La Vista Property. FORPD shall not pay any fees to District for the use of the La Vista
       Facilities and La Vista Property.

    3.5.    Agreement section 15 is modified to provide that any District termination of the
Agreement under that section shall not apply to FORPD’s right to use the La Vista Facilities and
La Vista Property and that, in the event of such a termination, the Agreement shall continue in
effect with respect to the La Vista Facilities and La Vista Property for the term of the Lease.

4. No Effect on Other Provisions. Except for the amendments in section 3, the remaining
provisions of the Joint Use Agreement are unaffected and remain in full force and effect.

                                  MEMORANDUM OF AGREEMENT

        This Memorandum of Agreement (“Memorandum”) is executed pursuant to the terms
and conditions of that certain Ground Lease and Construction Agreement (“Agreement”) by and
between the San Juan Unified School District, a public school district existing under the laws of
the State of California (“District”), and Fair Oaks Recreation and Parks District (“FORPD”). A
copy of the Agreement can be obtained at the offices of the District during regular business
hours.

        The purpose of this Memorandum is to help assure that the terms and conditions of the
Agreement inure to the benefit of and are binding upon all successors and assigns of FORPD and
District.

        This Memorandum may be executed in counterparts, each of which shall be deemed an
original and all of which together shall constitute one and the same Memorandum.

SUBJECT: Summer Learning                                                 CHECK ONE:

                                                                         Report:
DEPARTMENT: Division of Teaching and Learning                            Workshop:
                                                                         Recognition:
                                                                         Emergency Action:


ACTION REQUESTED:
The superintendent is recommending that the board hear the report on summer learning opportunities for the
summer of 2022.


RATIONALE/BACKGROUND:
The intent of this report is to highlight the innovative programs and opportunities that occurred this summer for
student learning. The Expanded Learning Opportunities (ELO) Grant and the Elementary and Secondary School
Emergency Relief Fund (ESSER III) allowed for supplemental instruction and support to students, including
those identified as needing academic, social-emotional, and other supports. This funding provided the district
the opportunity to implement a comprehensive and responsive learning recovery program as well as enrichment
opportunities to reconnect students to school communities. In an effort to be responsive with the allocations,
sites were also given local control to determine what actions would best meet the needs of students based on
conducting needs assessments. This summer our school sites, collaborating with community partners, created
high interest learning opportunities for students across the district. Each site was able to create and build
programs to meet the needs of all students.

ATTACHMENT(S):
A: Presentation

SUBJECT: Early Literacy Support Block (ELSB)                             CHECK ONE:
Grant Annual Update                                                      For Discussion:
                                                                         For Action:
                                                                         Report:
DEPARTMENT: Division of Teaching and Learning                            Workshop:
                                                                         Recognition:
                                                                         Emergency Action:


ACTION REQUESTED:
The superintendent is recommending that the board be updated on the progress of the Early Literacy Support Block grant
and approve the modification of the Literacy Action Plan to reflect these updates.

RATIONALE/BACKGROUND:
At the end of the second year of grant eligibility (Implementation Year 1), a local educational agency (LEA) with an
eligible school shall, as a non-consent agenda item at a regularly scheduled, publicly noticed meeting of its governing
board or body, provide an update on progress implementing the literacy action plan. The LEA may modify the literacy
action plan based on this update, consistent with the authorized uses of the grant funds.

                                                                  1




   Early Literacy Support Block Grant (ELSB)
             Background & Purpose
● Dyer-Kelly identified as one of 75 schools statewide with the
  highest percentage of students in grade three scoring at the
  lowest achievement standard level on the State Summative
  English Language Arts (ELA) assessment

● California Department of Education (CDE) awarded Dyer-
  Kelly $613,140 to develop and implement a three-year
  literacy action plan to include:
   ○ goals and actions to improve literacy instruction            2
   ○ identified metrics to measure progress toward the goals
   ○ planned expenditures that fund supplemental activities
      targeted for K-3




                                                                            1
                                                                                90
                      Planning Year
● 2020-2021 Dyer-Kelly Literacy Action Team conducted
  Needs Assessment and Root Cause Analysis

● Outcomes indicated:
  ○ A majority of Dyer-Kelly students were unable to
     decode complex, grade-level texts by the end of third
     grade
   ○ K-3 student needs in the following areas:
     ■ phonemic awareness instruction
     ■ oral reading fluency
                                                             3
     ■ site-wide common assessments
     ■ foundational skills
     ■ school-wide teaching strategies




               Four Areas of Focus
Based on Needs Assessment & Root Cause Analysis outcomes,
four areas of focus were identified:

● Literacy Coaching
● Language Essentials for Teachers of Reading & Spelling
   (LETRS) Learning
● Supplemental Curriculum Selection
● School Scheduling

BOARD OF EDUCATION
                                                                            MEETING DATE:            09/27/2022

SUBJECT: Public Hearing: Sufficiency of                                     CHECK ONE:
         Textbooks and Instructional Materials                              For Discussion:
                                                                            For Action:
                                                                            Report:
DEPARTMENT: Professional Learning and Curriculum Innovation                 Workshop:
                                                                            Recognition:
                                                                            Emergency Action:
ACTION REQUESTED:
The superintendent is recommending that the board hold a public hearing to discuss and adopt Resolution No.
4038 stating that each pupil in each school in the district has sufficient textbooks and instructional materials in
each subject that are consistent with the content and cycles of the curriculum framework adopted by the state
board.

RATIONAL/BACKGROUND:
Educational Code Section 60119 requires an annual public hearing and resolution regarding sufficient textbooks
and/or instructional materials. Public notice of this hearing was provided per education code provisions.

After reviewing textbooks throughout the district, Professional Learning and Curriculum Innovation is able to
certify that the district does have sufficient textbooks in each subject this year. Instructional materials funds and
lottery funds are used to purchase basic TK-12 textbooks and instructional materials in all curriculum areas.
Attached are the TK-12 board-adopted textbooks and instructional materials. Also attached is a brief explanation
of the methods followed to ensure sufficient textbooks and instructional materials.

ATTACHMENT(S):
A: Resolution No. 4038
B: Public notice
C: TK-12 board-adopted textbooks and instructional materials
D: Explanation of the methods followed to ensure sufficient textbooks and instructional materials

BOARD COMMITTEE ACTION/COMMENT:
N/A

                                                                                                                        95
                                                                                                                Attachment A
                                                 Resolution No. 4038
                                       Public Hearing Re: Education Code 60119
                                          TK-12 Instructional Materials Fund

WHEREAS, the Governing Board of San Juan Unified School District, in order to comply with the requirements of Education
Code Section 60119, held a public hearing on September 27, 2022, at 6:30 p.m., which is on or before the eighth week of school
and which did not take place during or immediately following school hours, and;

WHEREAS, the Governing Board provided at least 10 days notice of the public hearing posted in at least three public places
within the District that stated the time, place, and purpose of the hearing, and;

WHEREAS, the Governing Board encouraged participation by parents, teachers, members of the community, and bargaining unit
leaders in the public hearing, and;

WHEREAS, information provided at the public hearing and to the Governing Board at the public meeting detailed the extent to
which textbooks and instructional materials were provided to all students, including English Learners, in the District, and;

WHEREAS, the definition of “sufficient textbooks or instructional materials” means that each pupil has a textbook or
instructional materials, or both, to use in class and to take home, and;

WHEREAS, sufficient textbooks and instructional materials were provided to each student, including English learners, that are
aligned to the academic content standards and consistent with the cycles and content of the curriculum frameworks in the
following subjects: mathematics, science, history-social science, and English/language arts, including the English language
development component of an adopted program, and;

WHEREAS, sufficient textbooks or instructional materials were provided to each pupil enrolled in foreign language or health
classes, and;

WHEREAS, sufficient laboratory science equipment was provided for science laboratory classes offered in grades 9-12, inclusive;

THEREFORE BE IT RESOLVED that in the 2022 - 2023 school year, the San Juan Unified School District has provided each
pupil with sufficient textbooks and instructional materials aligned to the academic content standards and consistent with the cycles
and content of the curriculum frameworks.

IN WITNESS WHEREOF, the passage of the foregoing resolution in the manner and form prescribed by law, we, the members
of said Governing Board present and voting hereon, have hereunto set our hands this 27th day of September 2022.


                                                               Michael McKibbin, Ed.D., President


                                                                Zima Creason, Vice President

                                                                              Attachment B




                                  PUBLIC NOTICE

    NOTICE OF INTENT TO HOLD A PUBLIC HEARING TO DETERMINE WHETHER
    EACH PUPIL IN EACH SCHOOL IN THE SAN JUAN UNIFIED SCHOOL DISTRICT
    HAS, OR WILL HAVE PRIOR TO THE END OF THE FISCAL YEAR, SUFFICIENT
    TEXTBOOKS OR INSTRUCTIONAL MATERIALS, OR BOTH, IN EACH SUBJECT,
       THAT ARE CONSISTENT WITH THE CONTENT AND CYCLES OF THE
          CURRICULUM FRAMEWORK ADOPTED BY THE STATE BOARD

The San Juan Unified School District, to comply with Education Code section 60119, is
holding a public hearing to determine whether each pupil in each school in the District has,
or will have prior to the end of the fiscal year, sufficient textbooks or instructional materials,
or both, in each subject that are consistent with the content and cycles of the curriculum
framework adopted by the State Board of Education.

The public hearing before the Board of Trustees regarding this issue will be held on
September 27, 2022, starting at 6:30 p.m. in the Board Room at the San Juan Unified School
District office located at 3738 Walnut Avenue, Carmichael, CA.


Posted at:          San Juan Unified School District Office
                    Sylvan Public Library
                    Arden Public Library

Textbooks Professional Learning and Curriculum Innovation                                                                                                                                                            Last Updated 9/14/2022 Page 3 of 3
                                                                                                  Attachment D



                          Textbooks and Instructional Materials Sufficiency


Sufficiency of textbooks and instructional materials at all school sites is maintained through Business Support
Services. All school sites utilize the Follett system to manage and track their textbook assets. This system has
the ability to check out textbooks, facilitate the Williams reporting process, and view textbook inventory (site
and district-wide). All textbook requests are placed through the Follett system and fulfilled through the central
process at the district textbook warehouse. If the textbook is not available in the textbook warehouse, unused
copies are located at another school site through the Follett system by comparing class enrollment to the site
inventory of the associated textbook. Minimal quantities of textbooks are kept in stock in the warehouse.

Charter schools are not required to participate in the Williams requirements.

ACTION REQUESTED:
The superintendent is recommending the board discuss the proposed changes to Board Policy (BP) 0420.41,
Charter School Oversight, and its accompanying exhibit.


RATIONALE/BACKGROUND:
Board Policies are often updated to reflect new or updated practices in school systems. This board policy review
is focused on district oversight for charter schools. The changes to BP 0420.41 focus on district responsibilities in
their oversight and how the charter school needs to communicate with the district when requesting waivers from
the State Board of Education, services from the district, reporting to the state and making material revisions to the
Charter. The remainder of the document is reorganization and more precise language.

ATTACHMENT(S):
A: BP 0420.41 proposed changes
B: Exhibit 0420.41
